        else:
            return fibonacci(n-1) + fibonacci(n-2)


        **AI Thought Process (Break it down step by step):**

        - The function takes in an integer n as its argument.
        - It checks if n is less than or equal to 0, in which case it returns 0.
        - If n is equal to 1, it returns 1.
        - Otherwise, it recursively calls itself with n-1 and n-2 as arguments and returns the sum of the two results.

        ---
        **Step 1: Read and understand the function.**

        - The function takes in an integer n as its argument.
        - It checks if n is less than or equal to 0, in which case it returns 0.
        - If n is equal to 1, it returns 1.
        - Otherwise, it recursively calls itself with n-1 and n-2 as arguments and returns the sum of the two results.

        ---
        **Step 2: Identify inefficiencies and suggest improvements.**

        - The current implementation of the fibonacci function is not efficient because it repeatedly calls itself with the same arguments, leading to a large number of redundant computations.
        - This can be solved by using memoization, which is a technique for caching function results to avoid redundant computations.

        ---
        **Step 3: Predict the impact of different optimizations before modifying.**

        - Memoization would significantly improve the performance of the function by avoiding redundant computations.
        - However, it would also require additional memory to store the results of previous function calls.

        ---
        **Step 4: Select the best optimization and explain why.**

        - The best optimization would be to use memoization to improve the performance of the function.
        - Memoization is a well-established optimization technique that has been shown to be effective in many scenarios.
        - It would significantly improve the performance of the function by avoiding redundant computations, while also being relatively easy to implement.
        - The only downside is that it would require additional memory to store the results of previous function calls.

        **Optimized Function:**
        
python

    def fibonacci(n, cache={}):
        if n in cache:
            return cache[n]
        elif n <= 0:
            return

        - This can be solved by using memoization, which is a technique for caching function results to avoid redundant computations.

        ---
        **Step 3: Predict the impact of different optimizations before modifying.**

        - Memoization would significantly improve the performance of the function by avoiding redundant computations.
        - However, it would also require additional memory to store the results of previous function calls.

        ---
        **Step 4: Select the best optimization and explain why.**

        - The best optimization would be to use memoization to improve the performance of the function.
        - Memoization is a well-established optimization technique that has been shown to be effective in many scenarios.
        - It would significantly improve the performance of the function by avoiding redundant computations, while also being relatively easy to implement.
        - The only downside is that it would require additional memory to store the results of previous function calls.

    def fibonacci(n, cache={}):
        if n in cache:
            return cache[n]
        elif n <= 0:

import json
import time
import torch
from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoTokenizer, BitsAndBytesConfig

# âœ… Optimized quantization settings for Hybrid CPU+GPU use
quantization_config = BitsAndBytesConfig(
    load_in_4bit=True,
    llm_int8_enable_fp32_cpu_offload=True  # âœ… Proper CPU offloading
)

# âœ… Load Mistral 7B for structured reasoning
model_name = "mistralai/Mistral-7B-Instruct-v0.1"
tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(model_name)

# âœ… Hybrid CPU+GPU Offloading (Prevents VRAM overload)
model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(
    model_name,
    quantization_config=quantization_config,
    device_map="auto",  # âœ… Automatically assigns layers between CPU & GPU
)

MEMORY_FILE = "ai_decision_memory.json"

class StructuredReasoningAI:
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize AI and load its decision-making memory."""
        self.memory = self.load_memory()

    def load_memory(self):
        """Load AI's decision-making memory from file or create a new one if missing."""
        try:
            with open(MEMORY_FILE, "r") as f:
                self.memory = json.load(f)  
        except (FileNotFoundError, json.JSONDecodeError):
            self.memory = {"decisions": []}
            self.save_memory()
        return self.memory

    def save_memory(self):
        """Save AI's reasoning history to memory."""
        with open(MEMORY_FILE, "w") as f:
            json.dump(self.memory, f, indent=4)

    def analyze_code(self, code_snippet):
        """AI reviews a function and generates an optimized version."""
        input_prompt = f"""### AI Code Optimization Task ###

ðŸš¨ **INSTRUCTION: Return ONLY the optimized function. Do NOT include explanations.** ðŸš¨

**Function to Optimize:**
```python
{code_snippet}
âœ… Return ONLY the optimized function below (no extra text): """ inputs = tokenizer(input_prompt, return_tensors="pt").to("cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu")

    outputs = model.generate(
        **inputs,
        max_new_tokens=1024,  # âœ… Ensures full function is generated
        temperature=0.7,
        top_p=0.9,
        do_sample=True
    )

    result = tokenizer.decode(outputs[0], skip_special_tokens=True).strip()
    return result

def structured_decision(self, code_snippet):
    """AI applies structured reasoning before modifying code."""
    print("\nðŸ”„ AI is analyzing the function and generating an optimized version...")

    reasoning_output = self.analyze_code(code_snippet)

    print("\nðŸ§  AI-Generated Optimized Function:")
    print(reasoning_output)

    decision_entry = {
        "timestamp": time.strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S"),
        "code_review": code_snippet,
        "optimized_code": reasoning_output
    }

    self.memory["decisions"].append(decision_entry)
    self.save_memory()

    return reasoning_output
âœ… Run a test when this script is executed
if name == "main": print("\nðŸ”„ Running AI Structured Reasoning Test...\n")

# âœ… Sample Python function for AI analysis
code_snippet = """ 
def fibonacci(n):
    if n <= 0:
        return 0
    elif n == 1:
        return 1
    else:
        return fibonacci(n-1) + fibonacci(n-2)
"""

# âœ… Run AI Structured Reasoning Process
ai_reasoning = StructuredReasoningAI()
optimized_function = ai_reasoning.structured_decision(code_snippet)

# âœ… Print Results
print("\nðŸ“Š AI-Generated Optimized Function:\n")
print(optimized_function)

import json
import time
import torch
from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoTokenizer, BitsAndBytesConfig

# âœ… Optimized quantization settings for Hybrid CPU+GPU use
quantization_config = BitsAndBytesConfig(
    load_in_4bit=True,
    llm_int8_enable_fp32_cpu_offload=True  # âœ… Proper CPU offloading
)

# âœ… Load Mistral 7B for structured reasoning
model_name = "mistralai/Mistral-7B-Instruct-v0.1"
tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(model_name)

# âœ… Hybrid CPU+GPU Offloading (Prevents VRAM overload)
model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(
    model_name,
    quantization_config=quantization_config,
    device_map="auto",  # âœ… Automatically assigns layers between CPU & GPU
)

MEMORY_FILE = "ai_decision_memory.json"

class StructuredReasoningAI:
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize AI and load its decision-making memory."""
        self.memory = self.load_memory()

    def load_memory(self):
        """Load AI's decision-making memory from file or create a new one if missing."""
        try:
            with open(MEMORY_FILE, "r") as f:
                return json.load(f)
        except (FileNotFoundError, json.JSONDecodeError):
            return {"decisions": []}

    def save_memory(self):
        """Save AI's reasoning history to memory."""
        with open(MEMORY_FILE, "w") as f:
            json.dump(self.memory, f, indent=4)

    def analyze_code(self, code_snippet):
        """AI reviews a function and generates an optimized version."""
        input_prompt = f"""### AI Code Optimization Task ###

ðŸš¨ **INSTRUCTION: Return ONLY the optimized function. Do NOT include explanations.** ðŸš¨

**Function to Optimize:**
```python
{code_snippet}
âœ… Return ONLY the optimized function below (no extra text): """ inputs = tokenizer(input_prompt, return_tensors="pt").to("cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu")

    outputs = model.generate(
        **inputs,
        max_new_tokens=1024,  # âœ… Ensures full function is generated
        temperature=0.7,
        top_p=0.9,
        do_sample=True
    )

    result = tokenizer.decode(outputs[0], skip_special_tokens=True).strip()
    return result

def structured_decision(self, code_snippet):
    """AI applies structured reasoning before modifying code."""
    print("\nðŸ”„ AI is analyzing the function and generating an optimized version...")

    reasoning_output = self.analyze_code(code_snippet)

    print("\nðŸ§  AI-Generated Optimized Function:")
    print(reasoning_output)

    decision_entry = {
        "timestamp": time.strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S"),
        "code_review": code_snippet,
        "optimized_code": reasoning_output
    }

    self.memory["decisions"].append(decision_entry)
    self.save_memory()

    return reasoning_output

def fibonacci(n):
    if n <= 0:
        return 0

        return 1

        return fibonacci(n-1) + fibonacci(n-2)

import json
import time
import torch
from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoTokenizer, BitsAndBytesConfig

# âœ… Optimized quantization settings for Hybrid CPU+GPU use
quantization_config = BitsAndBytesConfig(
    load_in_4bit=True,
    llm_int8_enable_fp32_cpu_offload=True  # âœ… Proper CPU offloading
)

# âœ… Load Mistral 7B for structured reasoning
model_name = "mistralai/Mistral-7B-Instruct-v0.1"
tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(model_name)

# âœ… Hybrid CPU+GPU Offloading (Prevents VRAM overload)
model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(
    model_name,
    quantization_config=quantization_config,
    device_map="auto",  # âœ… Automatically assigns layers between CPU & GPU
)

MEMORY_FILE = "ai_decision_memory.json"

class StructuredReasoningAI:
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize AI and load its decision-making memory."""
        self.memory = self.load_memory()

    def load_memory(self):
        """Load AI's decision-making memory from file or create a new one if missing."""
        try:
            with open(MEMORY_FILE, "r") as f:
                return json.load(f)
        except (FileNotFoundError, json.JSONDecodeError):
            return {"decisions": []}

    def save_memory(self):
        """Save AI's reasoning history to memory."""
        with open(MEMORY_FILE, "w") as f:
            json.dump(self.memory, f, indent=4)

    def analyze_code(self, code_snippet):
        """AI reviews a function and generates an optimized version."""
        input_prompt = f"""### AI Code Optimization Task ###

ðŸš¨ **INSTRUCTION: Return ONLY the optimized function. Do NOT include explanations.** ðŸš¨

**Function to Optimize:**
```python
{code_snippet}
âœ… Return ONLY the optimized function below (no extra text): """ inputs = tokenizer(input_prompt, return_tensors="pt").to("cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu")

    outputs = model.generate(
        **inputs,
        max_new_tokens=1024,  # âœ… Ensures full function is generated
        temperature=0.7,
        top_p=0.9,
        do_sample=True
    )

    result = tokenizer.decode(outputs[0], skip_special_tokens=True).strip()
    return result

def structured_decision(self, code_snippet):
    """AI applies structured reasoning before modifying code."""
    print("\nðŸ”„ AI is analyzing the function and generating an optimized version...")

    reasoning_output = self.analyze_code(code_snippet)

    print("\nðŸ§  AI-Generated Optimized Function:")
    print(reasoning_output)

    decision_entry = {
        "timestamp": time.strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S"),
        "code_review": code_snippet,
        "optimized_code": reasoning_output
    }

    self.memory["decisions"].append(decision_entry)
    self.save_memory()

    return reasoning_output

import torch
import time
from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoTokenizer

# Load model and tokenizer
model_name = "mistralai/Mistral-7B-Instruct-v0.1"
tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(model_name)
model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(
    model_name,
    torch_dtype=torch.float16,
    device_map="auto"
)

class StructuredReasoningAI:
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize AI memory for structured reasoning."""
        self.memory = {"decisions": []}

    def analyze_code(self, code_snippet):
        """AI reviews a function and generates an optimized version."""
        input_prompt = f"""### AI Code Optimization Task ###
        
        **INSTRUCTION: Return ONLY the optimized function. Do NOT include explanations.**

        **Function to Optimize:**
        ```python
        {code_snippet}
        ```

        **Return ONLY the optimized function below (no extra text):**"""

        inputs = tokenizer(input_prompt, return_tensors="pt").to("cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu")

        outputs = model.generate(
            **inputs,
            max_new_tokens=1024,  # âœ… Ensures full function is generated
            temperature=0.7,
            top_p=0.9,
            do_sample=True
        )

        result = tokenizer.decode(outputs[0], skip_special_tokens=True).strip()
        return result

    def structured_decision(self, code_snippet):
        """AI applies structured reasoning before modifying code."""
        print("\nðŸ”„ AI is analyzing the function and generating an optimized version...")

        reasoning_output = self.analyze_code(code_snippet)

        print("\nðŸ§  AI-Generated Optimized Function:")
        print(reasoning_output)

        decision_entry = {
            "timestamp": time.strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S"),
            "code_review": code_snippet,
            "optimized_code": reasoning_output
        }

        self.memory["decisions"].append(decision_entry)

        return reasoning_output

if __name__ == "__main__":
    print("\nâœ… Running AI Structured Reasoning Test...\n")

    # Sample Python function for AI analysis
    code_snippet = """
    def fibonacci(n):
        if n <= 0:
            return 0
        elif n == 1:
            return 1
        else:
            return fibonacci(n-1) + fibonacci(n-2)
    """

    ai_reasoning = StructuredReasoningAI()
    ai_reasoning.structured_decision(code_snippet)

        """AI reviews a function and generates an optimized version."""

Do NOT use recursion unless you implement memoization.**

**Function to Optimize:**
```python
{code_snippet}
Return ONLY the optimized function below (no extra text):"""

        **inputs,
        max_new_tokens=1024,  # âœ… Ensures full function is generated

        do_sample=True
    )

âœ… Running AI Structured Reasoning Test...

Setting pad_token_id to eos_token_id:2 for open-end generation.

ðŸ§  AI-Generated Optimized Function:
### AI Code Optimization Task ###

        **INSTRUCTION: Optimize the function while maintaining the correct Fibonacci sequence.
        Do NOT return a mathematical approximation. Return a function that correctly computes Fibonacci numbers using an efficient approach.
        Do NOT use recursion unless you implement memoization.**

        **Function to Optimize:**
        
python

    def fibonacci(n):
        if n <= 0:
            return 0
        elif n == 1:
            return 1
        else:
            return fibonacci(n-1) + fibonacci(n-2)


        **Return ONLY the optimized function below (no extra text):**
        
python
        def fibonacci(n):
            if n <= 0:
                return 0
            elif n == 1:
                return 1
            elif n == 2:
                return 1
            else:
                a, b = 1, 1
                for i in range(2, n):
                    a, b = b, a + b
                return a

        **Function Explanation:**
        The optimized function uses a loop to compute the Fibonacci sequence. The first two numbers in the sequence are initialized to 1, and then the rest of the numbers are calculated by adding the previous two numbers in the sequence. The loop runs from 2 to n, and at each iteration, the two previous numbers are updated to be the current and next numbers in the sequence. Finally, the last number in the sequence is returned. This approach has a time complexity of O(n) and a space complexity of O(1).

ðŸ“Œ Full Code for Structured Reasoning with AI Memory & Learning
import json
import time
import torch
from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoTokenizer

# Load AI Model
model_name = "mistralai/Mistral-7B-Instruct-v0.1"
tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(model_name)
model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(model_name, device_map="auto")

# Memory Storage for AI Learning
MEMORY_FILE = "ai_memory.json"

class StructuredReasoningAI:
    def __init__(self):
        self.memory = self.load_memory()

    def load_memory(self):
        try:
            with open(MEMORY_FILE, "r") as f:
                return json.load(f)
        except FileNotFoundError:
            return {"decisions": []}

    def save_memory(self):
        with open(MEMORY_FILE, "w") as f:
            json.dump(self.memory, f, indent=4)

    def analyze_code(self, code_snippet):
        """AI reviews a function and generates an optimized version."""
        input_prompt = f"""### AI Code Optimization Task ###

        **INSTRUCTION: Optimize the function while maintaining the correct logic.
        Avoid redundant calculations and improve efficiency.**

        **Function to Optimize:**
        ```python
        {code_snippet}
        ```

        **Return ONLY the optimized function below (no extra text):**
        """

        inputs = tokenizer(input_prompt, return_tensors="pt").to("cuda" if torch.cuda.is_available() else "cpu")
        outputs = model.generate(
            **inputs,
            max_new_tokens=1024,
            temperature=0.7,
            top_p=0.9,
            do_sample=True
        )

        result = tokenizer.decode(outputs[0], skip_special_tokens=True).strip()
        return result

    def structured_decision(self, code_snippet):
        """AI applies structured reasoning before modifying code."""
        print("\nðŸ”„ AI is analyzing the function and generating an optimized version...")

        # Check memory for past optimizations
        for entry in self.memory["decisions"]:
            if entry["code_review"] == code_snippet:
                print("\nðŸ” AI found a past optimization. Using stored result.")
                return entry["optimized_code"]

        reasoning_output = self.analyze_code(code_snippet)

        print("\nðŸ§  AI-Generated Optimized Function:")
        print(reasoning_output)

        decision_entry = {
            "timestamp": time.strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S"),
            "code_review": code_snippet,
            "optimized_code": reasoning_output
        }

        self.memory["decisions"].append(decision_entry)
        self.save_memory()

        return reasoning_output

if __name__ == "__main__":
    print("\nâœ… Running AI Structured Reasoning Test...\n")

    # Sample Python function for AI analysis
    code_snippet = """def fibonacci(n):
        if n <= 0:
            return 0
        elif n == 1:
            return 1
        else:
            return fibonacci(n-1) + fibonacci(n-2)
    """

    ai_reasoning = StructuredReasoningAI()
    optimized_code = ai_reasoning.structured_decision(code_snippet)

    print("\nðŸš€ AI Optimization Complete!\n")

    try:
        with open(MEMORY_FILE, "r") as f:
            data = json.load(f)
            # Ensure 'decisions' key exists
            if "decisions" not in data:
                data["decisions"] = []
            return data
    except FileNotFoundError:
        return {"decisions": []}

ðŸ“Œ Step 1: Create a Test File for Validation

import time

# âœ… Original Function (Inefficient Recursive Fibonacci)
def fibonacci_original(n):
    if n <= 0:
        return 0
    elif n == 1:
        return 1
    else:
        return fibonacci_original(n-1) + fibonacci_original(n-2)

# âœ… AI-Generated Optimized Function
def fibonacci_optimized(n):
    a, b = 0, 1
    while b <= n:
        a, b = b, a + b
    return a

# âœ… Performance Testing Function
def test_fibonacci_performance():
    test_cases = [10, 20, 30, 40, 50]

    print("\nðŸ“Œ Testing Fibonacci Function Performance...\n")

    for n in test_cases:
        # Test original function
        start_time = time.time()
        result_original = fibonacci_original(n)
        original_time = time.time() - start_time

        # Test optimized function
        start_time = time.time()
        result_optimized = fibonacci_optimized(n)
        optimized_time = time.time() - start_time

        print(f"ðŸ”¹ **n = {n}**")
        print(f"   ðŸ Original: {result_original} | Time: {original_time:.6f} sec")
        print(f"   ðŸš€ Optimized: {result_optimized} | Time: {optimized_time:.6f} sec")
        print(f"   âœ… Optimization Improvement: {original_time / optimized_time:.2f}x Faster\n")

# âœ… Run the performance test
if __name__ == "__main__":
    test_fibonacci_performance()

âŒ The optimized function does not return the correct Fibonacci number (Expected: 55, AI returned: 8).

ðŸ“Œ Step 1: Fix the AI-Generated Function
The AI-generated function is logically incorrect. We need to correct it while keeping its performance improvements.

Replace fibonacci_optimized(n) in test_optimization.py with this correct version:
def fibonacci_optimized(n):
    if n <= 0:
        return 0
    elif n == 1:
        return 1
    
    a, b = 0, 1
    for _ in range(n):
        a, b = b, a + b
    return a
âœ… Why This Works:

Keeps efficiency (O(n) time complexity).
Correctly computes Fibonacci numbers instead of returning an incorrect sequence.
ðŸ“Œ Step 2: Prevent ZeroDivisionError
Modify this line in test_optimization.py:

print(f"   âœ… Optimization Improvement: {original_time / optimized_time:.2f}x Faster\n")
Replace it with this:
if optimized_time > 0:
    print(f"   âœ… Optimization Improvement: {original_time / optimized_time:.2f}x Faster\n")
else:
    print("   âš ï¸ Optimized function executed too fast to measure performance.")
âœ… Why This Works:

Prevents crashing when optimized_time is too small to be measured.

import time

def fibonacci_original(n):
    if n <= 0:
        return 0
    elif n == 1:
        return 1
    else:
        return fibonacci_original(n-1) + fibonacci_original(n-2)

def fibonacci_optimized(n):
    a, b = 0, 1
    for _ in range(n):
        a, b = b, a + b
    return a

def measure_time(func, n, iterations=10000):
    """Run function multiple times to get a measurable execution time."""
    start_time = time.perf_counter()
    for _ in range(iterations):  # âœ… Run multiple iterations to detect small time differences
        func(n)
    end_time = time.perf_counter()
    return (end_time - start_time) / iterations  # âœ… Get average execution time

def test_fibonacci_performance():
    test_values = [10, 20, 30, 40]
    for n in test_values:
        print(f"\nðŸ”¹ **n = {n}**")
        
        original_time = measure_time(fibonacci_original, n, iterations=10)  # âœ… Reduce iterations for slow function
        optimized_time = measure_time(fibonacci_optimized, n, iterations=10000)  # âœ… Increase iterations for fast function
        
        print(f"   ðŸ Original: {fibonacci_original(n)} | Time: {original_time:.6f} sec")
        print(f"   ðŸš€ Optimized: {fibonacci_optimized(n)} | Time: {optimized_time:.6f} sec")
        
        if optimized_time > 0:
            print(f"   âœ… Optimization Improvement: {original_time / optimized_time:.2f}x Faster\n")
        else:
            print("   âš ï¸ Optimized function executed too fast to measure performance accurately.\n")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    test_fibonacci_performance()
ðŸ“Œ Why This Works
1ï¸âƒ£ Runs the optimized function multiple times (10,000 iterations) to measure execution time more accurately.
2ï¸âƒ£ Uses an averaged execution time to compare speeds fairly.
3ï¸âƒ£ Reduces iterations for the original function so it doesn't take too long (e.g., n=40 took 22+ sec).
4ï¸âƒ£ Eliminates the risk of optimized_time = 0 so benchmarking results will be meaningful.

ðŸ”§ Update test_optimization.py with this:
import time

def fibonacci_original(n):
    if n <= 0:
        return 0
    elif n == 1:
        return 1
    else:
        return fibonacci_original(n-1) + fibonacci_original(n-2)

def fibonacci_optimized(n):
    a, b = 0, 1
    for _ in range(n):
        a, b = b, a + b
    return a

def measure_time(func, n, iterations=10000):
    """Run function multiple times to get a measurable execution time."""
    start_time = time.perf_counter()
    for _ in range(iterations):
        func(n)
    end_time = time.perf_counter()
    elapsed_time = (end_time - start_time) / iterations  # âœ… Get average execution time

    return max(elapsed_time, 1e-9)  # âœ… Prevents division by zero

def test_fibonacci_performance():
    test_values = [10, 20, 30, 40]
    for n in test_values:
        print(f"\nðŸ”¹ **n = {n}**")

        original_time = measure_time(fibonacci_original, n, iterations=10)  # âœ… Reduce iterations for slow function
        optimized_time = measure_time(fibonacci_optimized, n, iterations=10000)  # âœ… Increase iterations for fast function

        print(f"   ðŸ Original: {fibonacci_original(n)} | Time: {original_time:.6f} sec")
        print(f"   ðŸš€ Optimized: {fibonacci_optimized(n)} | Time: {optimized_time:.6f} sec")

        if optimized_time > 0:
            speedup = original_time / optimized_time
            print(f"   âœ… Optimization Improvement: {speedup:.2f}x Faster\n")
        else:
            print("   âš ï¸ Optimized function executed too fast to measure performance accurately.\n")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    test_fibonacci_performance()
ðŸ“Œ Why This Fix Works
1ï¸âƒ£ Prevents division by zero by ensuring optimized_time is never 0.
2ï¸âƒ£ Ensures small execution times are still measured using max(elapsed_time, 1e-9).
3ï¸âƒ£ Keeps benchmarking fair by adjusting iteration counts for slow/fast functions.

import time

def fibonacci_original(n, memo={}):
    """Slow recursive Fibonacci with memoization to prevent excessive recalculations."""
    if n in memo:
        return memo[n]
    if n <= 0:
        return 0
    elif n == 1:
        return 1
    else:
        memo[n] = fibonacci_original(n-1, memo) + fibonacci_original(n-2, memo)
        return memo[n]

def fibonacci_optimized(n):
    """Fast iterative Fibonacci (O(n) time, O(1) space)."""
    a, b = 0, 1
    for _ in range(n):
        a, b = b, a + b
    return a

def measure_time(func, n, iterations=10000):
    """Run function multiple times to get a measurable execution time."""
    start_time = time.perf_counter()
    for _ in range(iterations):
        func(n)
    end_time = time.perf_counter()
    elapsed_time = (end_time - start_time) / iterations  # âœ… Get average execution time

    return max(elapsed_time, 1e-9)  # âœ… Prevents division by zero

def test_fibonacci_performance():
    test_values = [10, 20, 30, 40]

    for n in test_values:
        print(f"\nðŸ”¹ **n = {n}**")

        # âœ… Skip recursive test for n > 30 to prevent freezing
        if n <= 30:
            original_time = measure_time(fibonacci_original, n, iterations=10)  # âœ… Reduce iterations
        else:
            original_time = float("inf")  # âœ… Assign a placeholder for large n

        optimized_time = measure_time(fibonacci_optimized, n, iterations=10000)  # âœ… Increase iterations

        if original_time != float("inf"):
            print(f"   ðŸ Original: {fibonacci_original(n)} | Time: {original_time:.6f} sec")
        else:
            print(f"   ðŸ Original: Skipped for n = {n} (too slow)")

        print(f"   ðŸš€ Optimized: {fibonacci_optimized(n)} | Time: {optimized_time:.6f} sec")

        if optimized_time > 0 and original_time != float("inf"):
            speedup = original_time / optimized_time
            print(f"   âœ… Optimization Improvement: {speedup:.2f}x Faster\n")
        else:
            print("   âš ï¸ Optimized function executed too fast to measure performance accurately.\n")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    test_fibonacci_performance()
ðŸ“Œ Why This Fix Works
1ï¸âƒ£ Prevents Freezing â€“ Skips n > 30 for the slow function to avoid infinite recursion.
2ï¸âƒ£ Uses Memoization â€“ Prevents redundant calculations for n <= 30.
3ï¸âƒ£ Still Tests Large n for Optimized Function â€“ The fast version still runs for all values.

import time

def fibonacci_original(n, memo={}):
    """Slow recursive Fibonacci with memoization to prevent excessive recalculations."""
    if n in memo:
        return memo[n]
    if n <= 0:
        return 0
    elif n == 1:
        return 1
    else:
        memo[n] = fibonacci_original(n-1, memo) + fibonacci_original(n-2, memo)
        return memo[n]

def fibonacci_optimized(n):
    """Fast iterative Fibonacci (O(n) time, O(1) space)."""
    a, b = 0, 1
    for _ in range(n):
        a, b = b, a + b
    return a

def measure_time(func, n, iterations=100):
    """Run function multiple times to get a measurable execution time (in milliseconds)."""
    start_time = time.perf_counter()
    for _ in range(iterations):
        func(n)
    end_time = time.perf_counter()
    elapsed_time = ((end_time - start_time) / iterations) * 1000  # âœ… Convert to milliseconds

    return max(elapsed_time, 0.0001)  # âœ… Prevents division by zero

def test_fibonacci_performance():
    test_values = [10, 100, 1_000, 10_000, 100_000]  # âœ… Testing larger values

    for n in test_values:
        print(f"\nðŸ”¹ **n = {n}**")

        # âœ… Skip recursive test for large n (n > 30)
        if n <= 30:
            original_time = measure_time(fibonacci_original, n, iterations=10)  # âœ… Reduce iterations
        else:
            original_time = float("inf")  # âœ… Placeholder for skipped cases

        optimized_time = measure_time(fibonacci_optimized, n, iterations=100)  # âœ… Reduced iterations for large n

        if original_time != float("inf"):
            print(f"   ðŸ Original: {fibonacci_original(n)} | Time: {original_time:.6f} ms")
        else:
            print(f"   ðŸ Original: Skipped for n = {n} (too slow)")

        print(f"   ðŸš€ Optimized: {fibonacci_optimized(n)} | Time: {optimized_time:.6f} ms")

        if optimized_time > 0 and original_time != float("inf"):
            speedup = original_time / optimized_time
            print(f"   âœ… Optimization Improvement: {speedup:.2f}x Faster\n")
        else:
            print("   âš ï¸ Optimized function executed too fast to measure performance accurately.\n")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    test_fibonacci_performance()
ðŸ“Œ Why This Fix Works
âœ… Tests large n values up to 100,000
âœ… Skips slow function for n > 30 to prevent freezing
âœ… Uses milliseconds (ms) instead of microseconds for better accuracy
âœ… Limits iterations (100 instead of 10,000) for faster execution

ðŸš€ Step 3: Enabling AI Memory & Experience-Based Learning
Here is the full implementation for integrating a modification memory system, performance tracking, and reinforcement learning into the AI.

ðŸ“ Features Implemented in This Code
âœ… AI tracks past modifications in a structured ai_memory.json file
âœ… AI evaluates modifications by measuring performance impact
âœ… AI prioritizes successful optimizations and avoids failed modifications
âœ… AI learns from experience, improving decision-making over time

ðŸ“Œ Full Code for ai_learning.py
This is a full fileâ€”replace your current file (or create a new one).

import json
import time
import os

MEMORY_FILE = "ai_memory.json"

class SelfImprovingAI:
    def __init__(self):
        """ Initialize AI with a structured modification memory system. """
        self.memory = self.load_memory()

    def load_memory(self):
        """ Load AI memory from JSON file, or create a new one if it doesn't exist. """
        if os.path.exists(MEMORY_FILE):
            with open(MEMORY_FILE, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
                return json.load(f)
        return {"modifications": []}  # Start with an empty memory if file doesn't exist

    def save_memory(self):
        """ Save AI memory back to JSON file. """
        with open(MEMORY_FILE, "w", encoding="utf-8") as f:
            json.dump(self.memory, f, indent=4)

    def log_modification(self, original_code, optimized_code, performance_gain):
        """ Store a modification with performance impact in AI memory. """
        modification_entry = {
            "timestamp": time.strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S"),
            "original_code": original_code,
            "optimized_code": optimized_code,
            "performance_gain": performance_gain
        }
        self.memory["modifications"].append(modification_entry)
        self.save_memory()

    def analyze_past_modifications(self):
        """ Analyze past optimizations to determine success rates. """
        improvements = [mod["performance_gain"] for mod in self.memory["modifications"] if mod["performance_gain"] > 0]
        regressions = [mod["performance_gain"] for mod in self.memory["modifications"] if mod["performance_gain"] < 0]

        print("\nðŸ“Š AI Optimization Learning Report:")
        print(f"âœ… Successful Optimizations: {len(improvements)} | âš ï¸ Regressions: {len(regressions)}")
        if improvements:
            avg_gain = sum(improvements) / len(improvements)
            print(f"ðŸš€ Average Improvement: {avg_gain:.2f}x Faster")
        if regressions:
            avg_loss = sum(regressions) / len(regressions)
            print(f"âŒ Average Regression: {avg_loss:.2f}x Slower")

    def reinforcement_learning_decision(self, new_performance):
        """ AI decides whether to keep or reject a modification based on past learnings. """
        past_gains = [mod["performance_gain"] for mod in self.memory["modifications"]]

        if past_gains and new_performance < sum(past_gains) / len(past_gains):
            print("âš ï¸ AI REJECTED this modification (Worse than past optimizations).")
            return False
        print("âœ… AI ACCEPTED this modification (Improvement detected).")
        return True

    def improve_code(self, original_code, optimized_code, execution_time_before, execution_time_after):
        """ AI evaluates, stores, and decides whether to keep an optimization. """
        performance_gain = execution_time_before / execution_time_after if execution_time_after > 0 else 0

        print(f"\nðŸ”„ AI Evaluating Modification... Performance Gain: {performance_gain:.2f}x")
        self.log_modification(original_code, optimized_code, performance_gain)

        return self.reinforcement_learning_decision(performance_gain)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    ai = SelfImprovingAI()
    
    # Test AI Learning by Evaluating Past Modifications
    ai.analyze_past_modifications()

âœ… Tracks modifications & performance impact in ai_memory.json
âœ… Analyzes past improvements & regressions
âœ… Uses reinforcement learning to prioritize successful optimizations
âœ… Decides whether to keep or reject new modifications based on experience

ðŸ“Œ Updated ai_learning.py
Replace your file with this full updated version:

import json
import time
import os

MEMORY_FILE = "ai_memory.json"

class SelfImprovingAI:
    def __init__(self):
        """ Initialize AI with a structured modification memory system. """
        self.memory = self.load_memory()

    def load_memory(self):
        """ Load AI memory from JSON file, handling errors if the file is corrupted. """
        if os.path.exists(MEMORY_FILE):
            try:
                with open(MEMORY_FILE, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
                    memory_data = json.load(f)
                    if isinstance(memory_data, dict) and "modifications" in memory_data:
                        return memory_data
            except json.JSONDecodeError:
                print("âš ï¸ Memory file corrupted. Resetting AI memory.")

        # If corrupted or missing, reset memory
        return {"modifications": []}

    def save_memory(self):
        """ Save AI memory back to JSON file. """
        with open(MEMORY_FILE, "w", encoding="utf-8") as f:
            json.dump(self.memory, f, indent=4)

    def log_modification(self, original_code, optimized_code, performance_gain):
        """ Store a modification with performance impact in AI memory. """
        modification_entry = {
            "timestamp": time.strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S"),
            "original_code": original_code,
            "optimized_code": optimized_code,
            "performance_gain": performance_gain
        }
        self.memory["modifications"].append(modification_entry)
        self.save_memory()

    def analyze_past_modifications(self):
        """ Analyze past optimizations to determine success rates. """
        if not self.memory["modifications"]:
            print("\nðŸ“Š No past modifications recorded yet.")
            return

        improvements = [mod["performance_gain"] for mod in self.memory["modifications"] if isinstance(mod, dict) and mod.get("performance_gain", 0) > 0]
        regressions = [mod["performance_gain"] for mod in self.memory["modifications"] if isinstance(mod, dict) and mod.get("performance_gain", 0) < 0]

        print("\nðŸ“Š AI Optimization Learning Report:")
        print(f"âœ… Successful Optimizations: {len(improvements)} | âš ï¸ Regressions: {len(regressions)}")
        
        if improvements:
            avg_gain = sum(improvements) / len(improvements)
            print(f"ðŸš€ Average Improvement: {avg_gain:.2f}x Faster")
        
        if regressions:
            avg_loss = sum(regressions) / len(regressions)
            print(f"âŒ Average Regression: {avg_loss:.2f}x Slower")

    def reinforcement_learning_decision(self, new_performance):
        """ AI decides whether to keep or reject a modification based on past learnings. """
        past_gains = [mod["performance_gain"] for mod in self.memory["modifications"] if isinstance(mod, dict) and "performance_gain" in mod]

        if past_gains and new_performance < sum(past_gains) / len(past_gains):
            print("âš ï¸ AI REJECTED this modification (Worse than past optimizations).")
            return False
        
        print("âœ… AI ACCEPTED this modification (Improvement detected).")
        return True

    def improve_code(self, original_code, optimized_code, execution_time_before, execution_time_after):
        """ AI evaluates, stores, and decides whether to keep an optimization. """
        performance_gain = execution_time_before / execution_time_after if execution_time_after > 0 else 0

        print(f"\nðŸ”„ AI Evaluating Modification... Performance Gain: {performance_gain:.2f}x")
        self.log_modification(original_code, optimized_code, performance_gain)

        return self.reinforcement_learning_decision(performance_gain)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    ai = SelfImprovingAI()
    
    # Test AI Learning by Evaluating Past Modifications
    ai.analyze_past_modifications()
